Let me synthesize what I've found and write the analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.\n\nHere's a summary of what I've found:\n\n1. **Request Arrival / Handler chain** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` - `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`):\n   - The handler chain is built in reverse order (innermost first wrapping)\n   - Order of execution (outer to inner):\n     1. `WithAuditInit` - sets up audit context\n     2. `WithPanicRecovery` - catches panics\n     3. `WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete` - routes requests\n     4. `WithRequestReceivedTimestamp` - records timing\n     5. `WithRequestInfo` - parses request into `RequestInfo` (resource, verb, namespace, name, etc.)\n     6. `WithLatencyTrackers` - measures latency\n     7. `WithTracing` - adds distributed tracing\n     8. CORS, HSTS, timeout, and wait group handlers\n     9. `WithAuthentication` - identifies the user, populates user.Info in context\n     10. `WithAudit` - creates audit event\n     11. `WithImpersonation` - handles user impersonation with authorization checks\n     12. `WithAuthorization` - enforces access control\n     13. The actual API handler\n\nThe authentication filter extracts credentials from the request, calls the configured authenticator, and on success removes the Authorization header while storing the authenticated user in the request context. There's also HTTP/2 mitigation for anonymous requests to address specific CVEs. The authorization filter then builds attributes from the request context and evaluates them against the configured authorizer to determine if the request should proceed.\n\nFor RBAC specifically, the authorizer uses a visitor pattern to check rules, and critically, if no rule matches it returns NoOpinion rather than Deny—this allows other authorizers in the chain to potentially allow the request. Even if RBAC encounters evaluation errors, those errors don't automatically block the request if another authorizer has already allowed it.\n\nThe rule resolver then walks through all ClusterRoleBindings to see which ones apply to the user (checking username, group membership, or ServiceAccount matches), and for each matching binding it retrieves the associated ClusterRole rules. In namespaced contexts, it also checks RoleBindings within that namespace using the same logic.\n\nThe authorizer chain itself starts with the superuser check for `system:masters`, then proceeds through Node, ABAC, Webhook, and RBAC authorizers in order, short-circuiting as soon as it hits an Allow or Deny decision.\n\nFor impersonation, the filter runs before authorization in the handler chain execution order, though I need to verify exactly how it interacts with the authorization wrapper.\n\nLooking at the handler chain construction, `WithAuthentication` wraps everything first (so runs last), then `WithAudit`, then `WithImpersonation`, then `WithAuthorization`, with the actual API handler at the core. This means impersonation executes before authorization sees the request. The impersonation filter checks if the original user is authorized to impersonate the target identity via an `impersonate` verb check, then modifies the user context before passing it to the authorization filter.\n\nThere's also a superuser bypass for `system:masters` group members that short-circuits the entire authorization chain with an allow decision. RBAC itself returns `DecisionNoOpinion` when rules don't match rather than denying, so it's permissive within the chain—the union authorizer only stops on explicit Allow or Deny decisions, and errors in rule resolution don't automatically block wires all filters together |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` | `WithAuthentication` filter — establishes caller identity |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` | `WithRequestInfo` filter — parses HTTP request into `RequestInfo` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` | `WithImpersonation` filter — validates and applies identity substitution |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` | `WithAuthorization` filter — the authorization gate; builds `AttributesRecord`, calls the authorizer chain |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go` | `WithAudit` filter — records decisions to the audit backend |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Core `Authorizer`, `Attributes`, `Decision`, `RuleResolver` interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` | `unionAuthzHandler` — chains multiple authorizers; short-circuits on Allow or Deny |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go` | `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` (system:masters bypass), `alwaysAllowAuthorizer`, `alwaysDenyAuthorizer` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/path/path.go` | Path-based allow-list authorizer for non-resource endpoints |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/user/user.go` | `user.Info` interface; well-known group constants (system:masters, system:authenticated, etc.) |\n| `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go` | `Config.New()` — instantiates RBAC/Node/ABAC/Webhook authorizers from configuration |\n| `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` | `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` — builds the union chain; supports hot-reload of authorization config |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` | `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()`, `RuleAllows()`, `RulesAllow()` — the core RBAC decision engine |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go` | `SubjectAccessEvaluator` — reverse lookup: which subjects can perform a given action |\n| `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` | `DefaultRuleResolver` — `VisitRulesFor()`, `appliesTo()`, `appliesToUser()`, `GetRoleReferenceRules()` |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/policy.go` | Default cluster roles and bindings installed at bootstrap |\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n### 1. Where API requests enter the authorization subsystem\n\nAll requests enter through `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`. The filter that routes requests into RBAC evaluation is `WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, `WithAuthorization` function, line 53). This filter reads the authenticated user from the request context, builds an `AttributesRecord` from request metadata, and calls `a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)` on the union authorizer chain.\n\nUntrusted input that reaches this entry point includes:\n- HTTP verb, URL path, query parameters (parsed into `RequestInfo`)\n- `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` HTTP headers\n- Bearer token / client certificate (feeds the authenticator)\n- Field/label selectors when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate is enabled (parsed in `GetAuthorizerAttributes`, lines 125–149)\n\n### 2. Where RBAC policy data enters the system\n\nRBAC policy objects (Roles, ClusterRoles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoleBindings) enter the system through the Kubernetes API itself and are stored in etcd. The RBAC authorizer reads them at decision time via **informer-backed listers** (cached watches):\n\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().Roles().Lister()` → `RoleGetter`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().RoleBindings().Lister()` → `RoleBindingLister`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().ClusterRoles().Lister()` → `ClusterRoleGetter`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().ClusterRoleBindings().Lister()` → `ClusterRoleBindingLister`\n\n(Wired in `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`, lines 123–128.)\n\nPolicy data is therefore **eventually consistent**: there is a brief window between a policy change being committed to etcd and being reflected in the in-memory cache.\n\n### 3. Places where untrusted input can influence authorization decisions\n\n| Input | Path | Risk |\n|-------|------|------|\n| Impersonation headers | `WithImpersonation` reads raw HTTP headers, parses them into `ObjectReference` structures, then fully substitutes the user identity in the request context before `WithAuthorization` runs | Identity substitution |\n| Field/label selectors in query string | `GetAuthorizerAttributes` optionally parses these into `AttributesRecord` when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` is on; a parse error sets `FieldSelectorParsingErr` but does **not** block the request | Selector injection, mis-parsed allow |\n| URL path | Parsed by `RequestInfoResolver.NewRequestInfo`; misrouting here (e.g., double-encoding) could produce incorrect resource/namespace/name in `AttributesRecord` | Attribute confusion |\n| ServiceAccount username format | `appliesToUser` in `rule.go` (line 281) calls `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername` for SA subjects — relies on correct username format (`system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>`) | Username spoofing if authn is misconfigured |\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### 1. Request Arrival\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`, line 1004) wraps the API handler with middleware in reverse execution order. The actual execution order is:\n\n```\nWithAuditInit\n  └─ WithPanicRecovery\n       └─ WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete\n            └─ WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\n                 └─ WithRequestInfo          ← parses URL → RequestInfo (verb, resource, ns, name, ...)\n                      └─ WithLatencyTrackers / WithTracing\n                           └─ timeout / wait-group / CORS / HSTS handlers\n                                └─ WithAuthentication  ← establishes identity\n                                     └─ WithAudit      ← opens audit event\n                                          └─ WithImpersonation  ← may replace identity\n                                               └─ WithAuthorization  ← ALLOW / DENY\n                                                    └─ API handler\n```\n\nKey data structures produced here:\n- `request.RequestInfo` (struct) — `IsResourceRequest`, `Verb`, `Namespace`, `Resource`, `Subresource`, `Name`, `APIGroup`, `APIVersion`\n- Stored in context via `request.WithRequestInfo(ctx, info)`\n\n### 2. Authentication\n\n`WithAuthentication` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`, line 46):\n- Calls `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` on a union authenticator (tokens, certificates, headers, etc.)\n- On success: strips `Authorization` header and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers to prevent header injection downstream\n- Stores `user.Info` (interface: `GetName()`, `GetUID()`, `GetGroups()`, `GetExtra()`) in context via `genericapirequest.WithUser(ctx, resp.User)`\n- CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigation: anonymous HTTP/2 clients receive `Connection: close` (when `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature gate is on)\n- If authentication fails, calls `failed.ServeHTTP` (returns HTTP 401); the request never reaches authorization\n\n### 3. Authorization Filter\n\n`WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, line 57):\n\n**Step 1 — Build attributes** (`GetAuthorizerAttributes`, line 100):\n```go\nattribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{}\nuser, _ := request.UserFrom(ctx)           // user.Info from authn\nrequestInfo, _ := request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx) // parsed URL\nattribs.User = user\nattribs.Verb = requestInfo.Verb\nattribs.Resource = requestInfo.Resource\nattribs.Namespace = requestInfo.Namespace\n// ... etc.\n```\nData type: `authorizer.AttributesRecord` implements `authorizer.Attributes` interface.\n\n**Step 2 — Call authorizer chain**:\n```go\nauthorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n```\n\n**Step 3 — Evaluate decision** (lines 79–96):\n```go\nif authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n    // pass through — NOTE: checked BEFORE error\n    handler.ServeHTTP(w, req)\n    return\n}\nif err != nil {\n    responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)   // 500\n    return\n}\n// DecisionNoOpinion or DecisionDeny → 403 Forbidden\nresponsewriters.Forbidden(...)\n```\n\n**Critical behavior**: The allow decision is checked before the error. A comment in the source reads: \"an authorizer like RBAC could encounter evaluation errors and still allow the request.\" This means if the superuser authorizer (or any earlier authorizer in the chain) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently swallowed.\n\nAudit annotations written: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` (allow/forbid) and `authorization.k8s.io/reason`.\n\n### 4. RBAC Evaluation\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) iterates authorizers in order. The chain always starts with `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` for `system:masters`, then proceeds through configured authorizers (Node, ABAC, Webhook, RBAC in operator-defined order).\n\n**`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 75):\n```go\nruleCheckingVisitor := &authorizingVisitor{requestAttributes: requestAttributes}\nr.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx,\n    requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n    requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n    ruleCheckingVisitor.visit)\nif ruleCheckingVisitor.allowed {\n    return authorizer.DecisionAllow, ruleCheckingVisitor.reason, nil\n}\n// NOT DecisionDeny — returns NoOpinion on denial\nreturn authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, reason, nil\n```\n\n**`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 179):\n1. Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects via the informer lister\n2. For each binding, calls `appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")` — checks username, groups, or SA format match\n3. If applies: calls `GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, clusterRoleBinding.RoleRef, \"\")` to retrieve `PolicyRule` slices from the referenced ClusterRole\n4. If namespace is non-empty: repeats above for `RoleBinding` objects in that namespace, resolving to either a Role or ClusterRole\n\n**`RuleAllows`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 178):\n```go\nfunc RuleAllows(requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n    if requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n        combinedResource := resource + \"/\" + subresource\n        return VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n               APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup) &&\n               ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource) &&\n               ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)\n    }\n    return VerbMatches(rule, verb) && NonResourceURLMatches(rule, path)\n}\n```\nWildcards (`*`) in policy rules are resolved in `rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches`, `APIGroupMatches`, `ResourceMatches`.\n\n**`appliesTo`** / **`appliesToUser`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 281):\n- `rbacv1.UserKind`: exact string match on `user.GetName()`\n- `rbacv1.GroupKind`: membership check in `user.GetGroups()`\n- `rbacv1.ServiceAccountKind`: `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(saNamespace, subject.Name, user.GetName())` — reconstructs the `system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>` username format\n\n### 5. Decision and Audit Logging\n\nThe union authorizer short-circuits and returns the first `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`. `DecisionNoOpinion` means \"continue to next authorizer.\" If all authorizers return `DecisionNoOpinion`, the final result is `DecisionNoOpinion`, which `WithAuthorization` treats as a 403.\n\nThe audit backend (configured via `--audit-policy-file`) receives:\n- `StageRequestReceived` on entry\n- `StageResponseStarted` / `StageResponseComplete` on exit\n- Annotations: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` and `authorization.k8s.io/reason` set by `WithAuthorization`\n- Impersonated user details if impersonation was performed (`audit.LogImpersonatedUser`)\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from request entry to authorization decision:\n\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` — `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` assembles the chain\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` — `WithRequestInfo` parses URL into `RequestInfo`\n3. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` — `WithAuthentication` → `user.Info` in context\n4. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` — `WithImpersonation` → may replace `user.Info` in context\n5. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` — `WithAuthorization` → calls authorizer chain\n6. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` — `Authorizer` interface, `AttributesRecord`, `Decision`\n7. `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` — `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` → `unionAuthzHandler`\n8. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` — iterates authorizers; first Allow/Deny wins\n9. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go` — `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` (always first)\n10. `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` — `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` → visitor pattern\n11. `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` — `DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor` → binding/role lookup, `appliesTo`\n12. Informer listers (backed by etcd watch cache) — supply `ClusterRoleBinding`, `RoleBinding`, `ClusterRole`, `Role` objects\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n**1. Authorization Bypass via system:masters**\n\nThe `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is unconditionally prepended to the authorizer chain (line 98–99 of `reload.go`):\n```go\nsuperuserAuthorizer := authorizerfactory.NewPrivilegedGroups(user.SystemPrivilegedGroup)\nauthorizers = append(authorizers, superuserAuthorizer)\n```\nAny authenticated principal whose `user.Info.GetGroups()` contains `\"system:masters\"` receives `DecisionAllow` for every request before RBAC is consulted. This is by design but represents a complete bypass of RBAC: there is no audit trail distinguishing a system:masters allow from an RBAC allow. If a compromised certificate can assert `system:masters` group membership (e.g., a leaked cluster admin certificate), no RBAC policy can block it.\n\n**2. Fail-Open on Rule Resolution Errors**\n\n`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` collects resolution errors but returns `DecisionNoOpinion` (not `DecisionDeny`) when no rule allows. The filter checks `DecisionAllow` before `err`. Combined with the union chain, if any earlier authorizer (e.g., a misconfigured webhook returning Allow) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently ignored — there is no \"fail closed\" behavior for the RBAC plugin itself. This could mask broken informer state or etcd connectivity issues.\n\n**3. Impersonation Attack Surface**\n\n`WithImpersonation` reads `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` headers and substitutes the authenticated user's identity before `WithAuthorization` runs. The filter does authorize each impersonation request against the original user, but:\n- Extra values are URL-decoded after lower-casing in `unescapeExtraKey` — a malformed encoding silently falls through (line 207: `return encodedKey`)\n- Group impersonation with `system:authenticated` or `system:unauthenticated` is accepted verbatim — an authorized impersonator can claim or drop these well-known groups by explicit specification\n- `system:masters` can be impersonated as a group if the requestor has `impersonate` on `groups` with the target name — granting full cluster admin to the downstream authorization\n\n**4. RBAC Privilege Escalation via Binding**\n\n`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` provides `ConfirmNoEscalation` (line 52) to prevent users from granting permissions they don't already hold. However, this function is only called during admission control for Role/ClusterRole creation — it is not part of the authorization path. A user with write access to `rolebindings` (but not `roles`) could bind themselves to an existing powerful ClusterRole without triggering escalation checks.\n\n**5. Policy Misconfiguration via Wildcards**\n\n`RuleAllows` matches `*` in verbs, API groups, resource names, and non-resource URLs. A ClusterRole with `verbs: [\"*\"], resources: [\"*\"], apiGroups: [\"*\"]` grants full cluster admin. Overly broad bootstrap roles (e.g., `cluster-admin` ClusterRole) bound to wide subjects (`system:authenticated`) represent a common misconfiguration path. There is no runtime enforcement checking whether wildcard usage is appropriate.\n\n**6. Informer Cache Staleness**\n\nThe RBAC authorizer reads from in-memory informer caches backed by etcd watch events. A role binding deletion or role restriction may take hundreds of milliseconds to propagate to all API server instances. During this window, revoked permissions remain in effect. This is inherent to the caching architecture but is a security consideration for time-sensitive revocations.\n\n**7. Authorization Config Hot-Reload Race**\n\n`reloadableAuthorizerResolver` uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` (line 70) to atomically swap the active authorizer chain when the authorization config file changes. In-flight requests at the moment of swap may be evaluated against the old chain. The reload loop polls once per minute and validates the new config before applying. There is no mechanism to drain in-flight requests before a reload, creating a brief consistency gap.\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n- **Authentication header stripping**: `WithAuthentication` deletes `Authorization` and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers after successful authentication, preventing downstream forgery.\n- **Impersonation gating**: Every impersonation target requires explicit `impersonate` verb authorization on the appropriate resource type before identity substitution.\n- **ConfirmNoEscalation**: Applied during admission for Role and ClusterRole write operations, preventing users from writing policies exceeding their own rights.\n- **Audit logging**: Every authorization decision (allow/deny) is annotated with decision and reason; impersonation is separately logged with the impersonated identity.\n- **Atomic config reload**: Authorization configuration changes are validated before applying and use atomic pointer swaps to avoid partial updates.\n- **HTTP/2 DoS mitigation**: Anonymous connections over HTTP/2 are forced to close after each request (CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigations gated on `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature flag).\n- **Bootstrap policy**: Default roles follow least-privilege where possible; high-privilege bindings (e.g., `cluster-admin`) are not granted to broad subjects.\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) defines these boundary behaviors:\n- **First Allow/Deny wins**: As soon as any authorizer returns `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`, the chain stops. A Webhook that returns Allow prevents RBAC from ever being consulted.\n- **No Deny from RBAC**: The RBAC plugin never returns `DecisionDeny` — only `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionNoOpinion`. This means RBAC cannot block requests that an earlier plugin allows.\n- **Node authorizer is first-class**: The Node authorizer runs before RBAC in the typical `Node,RBAC` configuration, restricting kubelet access using a dependency graph independent of RBAC policy.\n- **ABAC is additive**: ABAC returns `DecisionAllow` for matches and `DecisionNoOpinion` otherwise; it never denies. When combined with RBAC, ABAC can grant access that RBAC would not.\n\n### Authorizer Chain Interaction\n\nTypical production chain (order in `AuthorizationConfiguration.Authorizers`):\n\n```\nprivilegedGroupAuthorizer (system:masters — always first, hardcoded)\n  → Node authorizer (kubelet identity graph)\n  → RBAC authorizer (roles/bindings from etcd)\n  → Webhook (optional, external policy engine)\n```\n\nA `DecisionAllow` from `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` or Node short-circuits the rest of the chain. The RBAC authorizer is therefore effectively secondary to the system:masters check. Webhook authorizers are configurable with `failurePolicy: NoOpinion` (fail open) or `Deny` (fail closed), directly impacting security posture if the webhook is unreachable.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow is a multi-layer, pluggable system with clear separation between authentication (identity), impersonation (identity substitution), and authorization (policy enforcement). The core security posture is **default deny with explicit allow**: unauthenticated requests are rejected at the authentication layer, and requests without a matching RBAC policy receive HTTP 403.\n\n**Key findings:**\n\n1. **system:masters is an unconditional bypass.** It is enforced via `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` prepended to every authorizer chain, predates and supersedes all RBAC policy, and leaves no distinguishable audit trail. Compromise of any certificate asserting this group is a full cluster compromise with no RBAC-level mitigation.\n\n2. **RBAC never denies, only abstains.** All RBAC denials are expressed as `DecisionNoOpinion`, meaning earlier authorizers (superuser group, Node, Webhook) can grant access that RBAC policy would not. This is by design but means RBAC alone cannot implement explicit deny rules.\n\n3. **Impersonation is a significant attack surface.** Successfully impersonating `system:masters` as a group value grants complete cluster admin. The impersonation filter is correctly gated by authorization, but the authorization check uses the same pluggable chain — an ABAC or Webhook misconfiguration allowing the `impersonate` verb could lead to privilege escalation.\n\n4. **Policy data is eventually consistent.** Authorization decisions are made against an in-memory cache; revocations have a propagation delay during which stale permissions remain effective.\n\n5. **Field/label selector authorization is additive.** The `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate extends the `AttributesRecord` with parsed selectors, enabling more granular policy. Parse errors are carried through without blocking the request, which is safe (the error is an attribute of the record, not a hard failure) but requires authorizer implementations to handle the error case correctly.\n\nThe implementation is architecturally sound with defense-in-depth (authn → audit → impersonation authz → main authz), but the unconditional system:masters bypass and the fail-open nature of RBAC (NoOpinion not Deny) mean that the security of the overall system depends heavily on correct configuration of the authorizer chain ordering, webhook failure policies, and tight control over certificate issuance.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2014,"cache_read_input_tokens":67812,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2014,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"880f33bb-031b-41b5-b52f-872d3d77c2b5","uuid":"2f63c29b-d24f-46fc-90d7-c4767d85a5a5"}

The actual execution order is:\n\n```\nWithAuditInit\n  └─ WithPanicRecovery\n       └─ WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete\n            └─ WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\n                 └─ WithRequestInfo          ← parses URL → RequestInfo (verb, resource, ns, name, ...)\n                      └─ WithLatencyTrackers / WithTracing\n                           └─ timeout / wait-group / CORS / HSTS handlers\n                                └─ WithAuthentication  ← establishes identity\n                                     └─ WithAudit      ← opens audit event\n                                          └─ WithImpersonation  ← may replace identity\n                                               └─ WithAuthorization  ← ALLOW / DENY\n                                                    └─ API handler\n```\n\nKey data structures produced here:\n- `request.RequestInfo` (struct) — `IsResourceRequest`, `Verb`, `Namespace`, `Resource`, `Subresource`, `Name`, `APIGroup`, `APIVersion`\n- Stored in context via `request.WithRequestInfo(ctx, info)`\n\n### 2. Authentication\n\n`WithAuthentication` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`, line 46):\n- Calls `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` on a union authenticator (tokens, certificates, headers, etc.)\n- On success: strips `Authorization` header and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers to prevent header injection downstream\n- Stores `user.Info` (interface: `GetName()`, `GetUID()`, `GetGroups()`, `GetExtra()`) in context via `genericapirequest.WithUser(ctx, resp.User)`\n- CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigation: anonymous HTTP/2 clients receive `Connection: close` (when `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature gate is on)\n- If authentication fails, calls `failed.ServeHTTP` (returns HTTP 401); the request never reaches authorization\n\n### 3. Authorization Filter\n\n`WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, line 57):\n\n**Step 1 — Build attributes** (`GetAuthorizerAttributes`, line 100):\n```go\nattribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{}\nuser, _ := request.UserFrom(ctx)           // user.Info from authn\nrequestInfo, _ := request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx) // parsed URL\nattribs.User = user\nattribs.Verb = requestInfo.Verb\nattribs.Resource = requestInfo.Resource\nattribs.Namespace = requestInfo.Namespace\n// ... etc.\n```\nData type: `authorizer.AttributesRecord` implements `authorizer.Attributes` interface.\n\n**Step 2 — Call authorizer chain**:\n```go\nauthorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n```\n\n**Step 3 — Evaluate decision** (lines 79–96):\n```go\nif authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n    // pass through — NOTE: checked BEFORE error\n    handler.ServeHTTP(w, req)\n    return\n}\nif err != nil {\n    responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)   // 500\n    return\n}\n// DecisionNoOpinion or DecisionDeny → 403 Forbidden\nresponsewriters.Forbidden(...)\n```\n\n**Critical behavior**: The allow decision is checked before the error. A comment in the source reads: \"an authorizer like RBAC could encounter evaluation errors and still allow the request.\" This means if the superuser authorizer (or any earlier authorizer in the chain) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently swallowed.\n\nAudit annotations written: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` (allow/forbid) and `authorization.k8s.io/reason`.\n\n### 4. RBAC Evaluation\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) iterates authorizers in order. The chain always starts with `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` for `system:masters`, then proceeds through configured authorizers (Node, ABAC, Webhook, RBAC in operator-defined order).\n\n**`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 75):\n```go\nruleCheckingVisitor := &authorizingVisitor{requestAttributes: requestAttributes}\nr.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx,\n    requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n    requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n    ruleCheckingVisitor.visit)\nif ruleCheckingVisitor.allowed {\n    return authorizer.DecisionAllow, ruleCheckingVisitor.reason, nil\n}\n// NOT DecisionDeny — returns NoOpinion on denial\nreturn authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, reason, nil\n```\n\n**`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 179):\n1. Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects via the informer lister\n2. For each binding, calls `appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")` — checks username, groups, or SA format match\n3. If applies: calls `GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, clusterRoleBinding.RoleRef, \"\")` to retrieve `PolicyRule` slices from the referenced ClusterRole\n4. If namespace is non-empty: repeats above for `RoleBinding` objects in that namespace, resolving to either a Role or ClusterRole\n\n**`RuleAllows`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 178):\n```go\nfunc RuleAllows(requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n    if requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n        combinedResource := resource + \"/\" + subresource\n        return VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n               APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup) &&\n               ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource) &&\n               ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)\n    }\n    return VerbMatches(rule, verb) && NonResourceURLMatches(rule, path)\n}\n```\nWildcards (`*`) in policy rules are resolved in `rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches`, `APIGroupMatches`, `ResourceMatches`.\n\n**`appliesTo`** / **`appliesToUser`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 281):\n- `rbacv1.UserKind`: exact string match on `user.GetName()`\n- `rbacv1.GroupKind`: membership check in `user.GetGroups()`\n- `rbacv1.ServiceAccountKind`: `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(saNamespace, subject.Name, user.GetName())` — reconstructs the `system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>` username format\n\n### 5. Decision and Audit Logging\n\nThe union authorizer short-circuits and returns the first `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`. `DecisionNoOpinion` means \"continue to next authorizer.\" If all authorizers return `DecisionNoOpinion`, the final result is `DecisionNoOpinion`, which `WithAuthorization` treats as a 403.\n\nThe audit backend (configured via `--audit-policy-file`) receives:\n- `StageRequestReceived` on entry\n- `StageResponseStarted` / `StageResponseComplete` on exit\n- Annotations: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` and `authorization.k8s.io/reason` set by `WithAuthorization`\n- Impersonated user details if impersonation was performed (`audit.LogImpersonatedUser`)\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from request entry to authorization decision:\n\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` — `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` assembles the chain\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` — `WithRequestInfo` parses URL into `RequestInfo`\n3. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` — `WithAuthentication` → `user.Info` in context\n4. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` — `WithImpersonation` → may replace `user.Info` in context\n5. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` — `WithAuthorization` → calls authorizer chain\n6. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` — `Authorizer` interface, `AttributesRecord`, `Decision`\n7. `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` — `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` → `unionAuthzHandler`\n8. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` — iterates authorizers; first Allow/Deny wins\n9. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go` — `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` (always first)\n10. `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` — `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` → visitor pattern\n11. `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` — `DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor` → binding/role lookup, `appliesTo`\n12. Informer listers (backed by etcd watch cache) — supply `ClusterRoleBinding`, `RoleBinding`, `ClusterRole`, `Role` objects\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n**1. Authorization Bypass via system:masters**\n\nThe `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is unconditionally prepended to the authorizer chain (line 98–99 of `reload.go`):\n```go\nsuperuserAuthorizer := authorizerfactory.NewPrivilegedGroups(user.SystemPrivilegedGroup)\nauthorizers = append(authorizers, superuserAuthorizer)\n```\nAny authenticated principal whose `user.Info.GetGroups()` contains `\"system:masters\"` receives `DecisionAllow` for every request before RBAC is consulted. This is by design but represents a complete bypass of RBAC: there is no audit trail distinguishing a system:masters allow from an RBAC allow. If a compromised certificate can assert `system:masters` group membership (e.g., a leaked cluster admin certificate), no RBAC policy can block it.\n\n**2. Fail-Open on Rule Resolution Errors**\n\n`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` collects resolution errors but returns `DecisionNoOpinion` (not `DecisionDeny`) when no rule allows. The filter checks `DecisionAllow` before `err`. Combined with the union chain, if any earlier authorizer (e.g., a misconfigured webhook returning Allow) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently ignored — there is no \"fail closed\" behavior for the RBAC plugin itself. This could mask broken informer state or etcd connectivity issues.\n\n**3. Impersonation Attack Surface**\n\n`WithImpersonation` reads `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` headers and substitutes the authenticated user's identity before `WithAuthorization` runs. The filter does authorize each impersonation request against the original user, but:\n- Extra values are URL-decoded after lower-casing in `unescapeExtraKey` — a malformed encoding silently falls through (line 207: `return encodedKey`)\n- Group impersonation with `system:authenticated` or `system:unauthenticated` is accepted verbatim — an authorized impersonator can claim or drop these well-known groups by explicit specification\n- `system:masters` can be impersonated as a group if the requestor has `impersonate` on `groups` with the target name — granting full cluster admin to the downstream authorization\n\n**4. RBAC Privilege Escalation via Binding**\n\n`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` provides `ConfirmNoEscalation` (line 52) to prevent users from granting permissions they don't already hold. However, this function is only called during admission control for Role/ClusterRole creation — it is not part of the authorization path. A user with write access to `rolebindings` (but not `roles`) could bind themselves to an existing powerful ClusterRole without triggering escalation checks.\n\n**5. Policy Misconfiguration via Wildcards**\n\n`RuleAllows` matches `*` in verbs, API groups, resource names, and non-resource URLs. A ClusterRole with `verbs: [\"*\"], resources: [\"*\"], apiGroups: [\"*\"]` grants full cluster admin. Overly broad bootstrap roles (e.g., `cluster-admin` ClusterRole) bound to wide subjects (`system:authenticated`) represent a common misconfiguration path. There is no runtime enforcement checking whether wildcard usage is appropriate.\n\n**6. Informer Cache Staleness**\n\nThe RBAC authorizer reads from in-memory informer caches backed by etcd watch events. A role binding deletion or role restriction may take hundreds of milliseconds to propagate to all API server instances. During this window, revoked permissions remain in effect. This is inherent to the caching architecture but is a security consideration for time-sensitive revocations.\n\n**7. Authorization Config Hot-Reload Race**\n\n`reloadableAuthorizerResolver` uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` (line 70) to atomically swap the active authorizer chain when the authorization config file changes. In-flight requests at the moment of swap may be evaluated against the old chain. The reload loop polls once per minute and validates the new config before applying. There is no mechanism to drain in-flight requests before a reload, creating a brief consistency gap.\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n- **Authentication header stripping**: `WithAuthentication` deletes `Authorization` and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers after successful authentication, preventing downstream forgery.\n- **Impersonation gating**: Every impersonation target requires explicit `impersonate` verb authorization on the appropriate resource type before identity substitution.\n- **ConfirmNoEscalation**: Applied during admission for Role and ClusterRole write operations, preventing users from writing policies exceeding their own rights.\n- **Audit logging**: Every authorization decision (allow/deny) is annotated with decision and reason; impersonation is separately logged with the impersonated identity.\n- **Atomic config reload**: Authorization configuration changes are validated before applying and use atomic pointer swaps to avoid partial updates.\n- **HTTP/2 DoS mitigation**: Anonymous connections over HTTP/2 are forced to close after each request (CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigations gated on `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature flag).\n- **Bootstrap policy**: Default roles follow least-privilege where possible; high-privilege bindings (e.g., `cluster-admin`) are not granted to broad subjects.\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) defines these boundary behaviors:\n- **First Allow/Deny wins**: As soon as any authorizer returns `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`, the chain stops. A Webhook that returns Allow prevents RBAC from ever being consulted.\n- **No Deny from RBAC**: The RBAC plugin never returns `DecisionDeny` — only `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionNoOpinion`. This means RBAC cannot block requests that an earlier plugin allows.\n- **Node authorizer is first-class**: The Node authorizer runs before RBAC in the typical `Node,RBAC` configuration, restricting kubelet access using a dependency graph independent of RBAC policy.\n- **ABAC is additive**: ABAC returns `DecisionAllow` for matches and `DecisionNoOpinion` otherwise; it never denies. When combined with RBAC, ABAC can grant access that RBAC would not.\n\n### Authorizer Chain Interaction\n\nTypical production chain (order in `AuthorizationConfiguration.Authorizers`):\n\n```\nprivilegedGroupAuthorizer (system:masters — always first, hardcoded)\n  → Node authorizer (kubelet identity graph)\n  → RBAC authorizer (roles/bindings from etcd)\n  → Webhook (optional, external policy engine)\n```\n\nA `DecisionAllow` from `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` or Node short-circuits the rest of the chain. The RBAC authorizer is therefore effectively secondary to the system:masters check. Webhook authorizers are configurable with `failurePolicy: NoOpinion` (fail open) or `Deny` (fail closed), directly impacting security posture if the webhook is unreachable.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow is a multi-layer, pluggable system with clear separation between authentication (identity), impersonation (identity substitution), and authorization (policy enforcement). The core security posture is **default deny with explicit allow**: unauthenticated requests are rejected at the authentication layer, and requests without a matching RBAC policy receive HTTP 403.\n\n**Key findings:**\n\n1. **system:masters is an unconditional bypass.** It is enforced via `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` prepended to every authorizer chain, predates and supersedes all RBAC policy, and leaves no distinguishable audit trail. Compromise of any certificate asserting this group is a full cluster compromise with no RBAC-level mitigation.\n\n2. **RBAC never denies, only abstains.** All RBAC denials are expressed as `DecisionNoOpinion`, meaning earlier authorizers (superuser group, Node, Webhook) can grant access that RBAC policy would not. This is by design but means RBAC alone cannot implement explicit deny rules.\n\n3. **Impersonation is a significant attack surface.** Successfully impersonating `system:masters` as a group value grants complete cluster admin. The impersonation filter is correctly gated by authorization, but the authorization check uses the same pluggable chain — an ABAC or Webhook misconfiguration allowing the `impersonate` verb could lead to privilege escalation.\n\n4. **Policy data is eventually consistent.** Authorization decisions are made against an in-memory cache; revocations have a propagation delay during which stale permissions remain effective.\n\n5. **Field/label selector authorization is additive.** The `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate extends the `AttributesRecord` with parsed selectors, enabling more granular policy. Parse errors are carried through without blocking the request, which is safe (the error is an attribute of the record, not a hard failure) but requires authorizer implementations to handle the error case correctly.\n\nThe implementation is architecturally sound with defense-in-depth (authn → audit → impersonation authz → main authz), but the unconditional system:masters bypass and the fail-open nature of RBAC (NoOpinion not Deny) mean that the security of the overall system depends heavily on correct configuration of the authorizer chain ordering, webhook failure policies, and tight control over certificate issuance.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
